        </a>

     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       So Paulo
      </b>
      (
      <span class="nowrap">
       <span class="IPA nopopups">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
         /
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
          <span title="// secondary stress follows">
           
          </span>
          <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
           s
          </span>
          <span title="/a/ 'ou' in 'pout'">
           a
          </span>
         </span>
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
          <span title="// primary stress follows">
           
          </span>
          <span title="'p' in 'pie'">
           p
          </span>
          <span title="/a/ 'ou' in 'pout'">
           a
          </span>
          <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
           l
          </span>
          <span title="/o/ long 'o' in 'code'">
           o
          </span>
         </span>
         /
        </a>
       </span>
      </span>
      ;
      <small>
       Portuguese pronunciation:
      </small>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">
        [sw pawlu]
       </a>
      </span>
      <small class="nowrap metadata">
       (
       <a href="/wiki/File:Br-SaoPaulo.ogg" title="File:Br-SaoPaulo.ogg">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/>
       </a>
       <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/Br-SaoPaulo.ogg" title="Br-SaoPaulo.ogg">
        listen
       </a>
       )
      </small>
      ;
      <i>
       Saint Paul
      </i>
      ) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">
       municipality
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolis" title="Metropolis">
       metropolis
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">
       global city
      </a>
      located in
      <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Southeast Region, Brazil">
       southeastern
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      . It is the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_in_Brazil" title="List of largest cities in Brazil">
       most populous city
      </a>
      in Brazil,
      <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_in_the_Americas" title="Largest cities in the Americas">
       in the Americas
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
       in the western hemisphere
      </a>
      and the world's
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population" title="List of cities proper by population">
       twelfth largest city by population
      </a>
      . The metropolis is anchor to the
      <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater So Paulo">
       So Paulo metropolitan area
      </a>
      , ranked as the most populous metropolitan area in Brazil,
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_Americas" title="List of metropolitan areas in the Americas">
       the second
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
       Americas
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">
       the seventh
      </a>
      in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo is the capital of
      <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">
       the state
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="So Paulo (state)">
       So Paulo
      </a>
      , Brazil's
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_states_by_population" title="List of Brazilian states by population">
       most populous
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_federative_units_by_gross_domestic_product" title="List of Brazilian federative units by gross domestic product">
       wealthiest
      </a>
      state. It exerts strong regional influence in commerce, finance, arts and entertainment and a strong international influence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The name of the city honors
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">
       Saint Paul of Tarsus
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Having the largest economy by
      <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
       GDP
      </a>
      in Latin America and Southern Hemisphere,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the city is home to the
      <a href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">
       So Paulo Stock Exchange
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">
       Paulista Avenue
      </a>
      is the economic core of So Paulo. The metropolis is also home to several of
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Brazil" title="List of tallest buildings in Brazil">
       the tallest buildings in Brazil
      </a>
      , including the building
      <a href="/wiki/Mirante_do_Vale" title="Mirante do Vale">
       Mirante do Vale
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edif%C3%ADcio_It%C3%A1lia" title="Edifcio Itlia">
       Edifcio Itlia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Altino_Arantes_Building" title="Altino Arantes Building">
       Banespa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Centro_Empresarial_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_Unidas" title="Centro Empresarial Naes Unidas">
       North Tower
      </a>
      and many others. The city has significant cultural, economic and political influence both nationally and internationally. It is home to several important monuments, parks and museums such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Latin_America_Memorial" title="Latin America Memorial">
       Latin American Memorial
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">
       Ibirapuera Park
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Museu_Paulista" title="Museu Paulista">
       Museum of Ipiranga
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Art" title="So Paulo Museum of Art">
       So Paulo Museum of Art
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">
       Museum of the Portuguese Language
      </a>
      . The city holds high profile events, like the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="So Paulo Art Biennial">
       So Paulo Art Biennial
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="Brazilian Grand Prix">
       Brazilian Grand Prix
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Fashion_Week" title="So Paulo Fashion Week">
       So Paulo Fashion Week
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Brasil_Open" title="Brasil Open">
       ATP Brasil Open
      </a>
      . So Paulo hosts the world's largest
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="So Paulo Gay Pride Parade">
       gay pride parade
      </a>
      . It is also the headquarters of the
      <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Brazil" title="Television in Brazil">
       Brazilian television
      </a>
      networks
      <a href="/wiki/Rede_Record" title="Rede Record">
       Record
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rede_Bandeirantes" title="Rede Bandeirantes">
       Band
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rede_Gazeta" title="Rede Gazeta">
       Gazeta
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      So Paulo is a
      <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">
       cosmopolitan
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Melting_pot" title="Melting pot">
       melting pot
      </a>
      city, home to the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Italian_diaspora" title="Italian diaspora">
       Italian
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_diaspora" title="Arab diaspora">
       Arab
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_diaspora" title="Japanese diaspora">
       Japanese
      </a>
      diasporas, with examples including
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_enclave" title="Ethnic enclave">
       ethnic neighborhoods
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Bixiga" title="Bixiga">
       Bixiga
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="extiw" href="//pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercado_(bairro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="pt:Mercado (bairro de So Paulo)">
       Mercado
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Liberdade_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Liberdade (district of So Paulo)">
       Liberdade
      </a>
      respectively. People from the city are known as
      <i>
       paulistanos
      </i>
      , while
      <i>
       paulistas
      </i>
      designates anyone from
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="So Paulo (state)">
       the state
      </a>
      , including the
      <i>
       paulistanos
      </i>
      . The city's
      <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
       Latin
      </a>
      motto, which it has shared with
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Brazilian battleship So Paulo">
       the battleship
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_aircraft_carrier_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(A12)" title="Brazilian aircraft carrier So Paulo (A12)">
       the aircraft carrier
      </a>
      named after it, is
      <i>
       Non ducor, duco
      </i>
      , which translates as "I am not led, I lead."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The city, which is also colloquially known as
      <i>
       Sampa
      </i>
      or
      <i>
       Terra da Garoa
      </i>
      (Land of Drizzle), is known for its unreliable weather, the size of its helicopter fleet, its architecture, gastronomy, severe traffic congestion and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="List of tallest buildings in So Paulo">
       skyscrapers
      </a>
      . According to a report from 2011, So Paulo was expected to have the third highest economic growth in the world between 2011 and 2025, after
      <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
       London
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
       Mexico City
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo was one of the host cities of the
      <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">
       1950
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">
       2014 FIFA World Cup
      </a>
      . Additionally, the city hosted the
      <a href="/wiki/1963_Pan_American_Games" title="1963 Pan American Games">
       IV Pan American Games
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Indy_300" title="So Paulo Indy 300">
       So Paulo Indy 300
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Timeline of So Paulo">
       Timeline of So Paulo
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">
       Colonial period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_1913.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="511" data-file-width="800" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1913.jpg/220px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1913.jpg/330px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1913.jpg/440px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1913.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         Founding of So Paulo
        </i>
        , 1913 painting by Antonio Parreiras
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Portuguese village of
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_dos_Campos_de_Piratininga" title="So Paulo dos Campos de Piratininga">
       So Paulo dos Campos de Piratininga
      </a>
      was marked by the founding of the
      <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio" title="Ptio do Colgio">
       Colgio de So Paulo de Piratininga
      </a>
      on January 25, 1554. The
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
       Jesuit
      </a>
      college of twelve priests included Manuel da Nbrega and Jos de Anchieta, and their structure was located on top of a steep hill between the rivers
      <a href="/wiki/Anhangaba%C3%BA_River" title="Anhangaba River">
       Anhangaba
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tamanduate%C3%AD_River" title="Tamanduate River">
       Tamanduate
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawrence183_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lawrence183-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      They first had a small structure built of rammed earth, made by the Indian workers in their traditional style. The priests wanted to evangelize - teach (
      <a href="/wiki/Catechesis" title="Catechesis">
       catechesis
      </a>
      ) the Indians who lived in the Plateau region of Piratininga and convert them to Christianity. The site was separated from the coast by the
      <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">
       Serra do Mar
      </a>
      , called by the Indians
      <i>
       Serra Paranapiacaba.
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The name of the college was chosen as it was founded on the celebration of the conversion of the Apostle
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_of_Tarsus" title="Paul of Tarsus">
       Paul of Tarsus
      </a>
      . Father Jos de Anchieta wrote this account in a letter to the Society of Jesus:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       The settlement of the region's Courtyard of the College began in 1560. During the visit of Mem de S, Governor-General of Brazil, the Captaincy of So Vicente, he ordered the transfer of the population of the Village of Santo Andr da Borda do Campo to the vicinity of the college. It was then named "College of St. Paul Piratininga". The new location was on a steep hill adjacent to a large wetland, the lowland do Carmo. It offered better protection from attacks by local Indian groups. It was renamed Vila de So Paulo, belonging to the Captaincy of So Vicente.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      For the next two centuries, So Paulo developed as a poor and isolated village that survived largely through the mostly native population's cultivation of subsistence crops. For a long time, So Paulo was the only village in Brazil's interior, as travel was too difficult to reach the area. Mem de S forbade colonists to use the "Path Piraiqu" (Piaaguera today), because of frequent Indian raids along it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 22, 1681, the Marquis de Cascais, the donee of the Captaincy of So Vicente, moved the capital to the village of St. Paul, designating it the "Head of the captaincy." The new capital was established in April 23, 1683, with public celebrations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bandeirantes">
       The Bandeirantes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Bandeirantes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">
       Bandeirantes
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3953" data-file-width="7940" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/220px-P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/330px-P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/440px-P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Courtyard of the College,
        <i>
         Patio do Colgio
        </i>
        , in the Historic Center of So Paulo. At this location, the city was founded in 1554. The current building is a reconstruction made in the late 20th century, based on the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
         Jesuit
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">
         college
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Church_(building)" title="Church (building)">
         church
        </a>
        that were erected at the site in 1653.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the 17th century, So Paulo was one of the poorest regions of the Portuguese colony. It was also the center of interior colonial development. Because they were extremely poor, the Paulistas could not afford to buy
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
       African slaves
      </a>
      , as did other Portuguese colonists. The discovery of gold in the region of
      <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">
       Minas Gerais
      </a>
      , in the 1690s, brought attention and new settlers to So Paulo. The Captaincy of So Paulo and Minas do Ouro was created in November 3, 1709, when the Portuguese crown purchased the Captaincies of So Paulo and Santo Amaro from the former grantees.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Conveniently located in the country, up the steep
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">
        Serra do Mar
       </a>
      </i>
      sea ridge when travelling from
      <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, So Paulo">
       Santos
      </a>
      , while also not too far from the coastline, So Paulo became a safe place to stay for tired travellers. The town became a centre for the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">
        bandeirantes
       </a>
      </i>
      , intrepid explorers who marched into unknown lands in search for gold, diamonds, precious stones, and Indians to make slaves of. The
      <i>
       bandeirantes
      </i>
      , which could be translated as "flag-bearers" or "flag-followers", organized excursions into the land with the primary purpose of profit and the expansion of territory for the Portuguese crown. Trade grew from the local markets and from providing food and accommodation for explorers. The
      <i>
       bandeirantes
      </i>
      eventually became politically powerful as a group, and were considered responsible for the expulsion of the Jesuits from the city of So Paulo in 1640, after a series of conflicts between the Jesuits and the
      <i>
       bandeirantes
      </i>
      over the trade of Indian slaves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 11, 1711, the town of So Paulo was elevated to city status. Around the 1720s, gold was found by the pioneers in the regions near what are now Cuiab and Goiania. The Portuguese expanded their Brazilian territory beyond the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tordesillas_Line" title="Tordesillas Line">
       Tordesillas Line
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      When the gold ran out in the late 18th century, So Paulo shifted to growing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">
       sugar cane
      </a>
      , which spread through the interior of the Captaincy. The sugar was exported through the
      <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santos" title="Port of Santos">
       Port of Santos
      </a>
      . At that time, the first modern highway between So Paulo and the coast was constructed and named the Walk of Lorraine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nowadays, the estate that is home to the Governor of the State of So Paulo, located in the city of So Paulo, is called the
      <i>
       Palcio dos Bandeirantes
      </i>
      (Palace of Bandeirantes), in the neighbourhood of Morumbi.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Period">
       Imperial Period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Imperial Period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">
       Empire of Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg/220px-Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg/330px-Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg/440px-Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Independence_of_Brazil" title="Monument to the Independence of Brazil">
         Monument to Independence
        </a>
        in Independence Park, located at the place where then-
        <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">
         Prince Pedro
        </a>
        proclaimed the
        <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">
         independence of Brazil
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After Brazil became independent from Portugal in 1823, as declared by
      <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">
       Dom Pedro I
      </a>
      where the Monument of Ipiranga is located, he named So Paulo as an Imperial City. In 1827, a law school was founded at the Convent of So Francisco, these days a part of the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of So Paulo">
       University of So Paulo
      </a>
      . The influx of students and teachers gave a new impetus to the city's growth, thanks to which the city became the
      <i>
       Imperial City and Borough of Students of St. Paul of Piratininga
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The expansion of
      <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Brazil" title="Coffee production in Brazil">
       coffee production
      </a>
      was a major factor in the growth of So Paulo, as it became the region's chief export crop and yielded good revenue. It was cultivated initially in the Vale do Paraba (
      <i>
       Paraba Valley
      </i>
      ) region in the East of the State of So Paulo, and later on in the regions of Campinas, Rio Claro, So Carlos and Ribeiro Preto.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From 1869 onwards, So Paulo was connected to the port of Santos by the Railroad Santos-Jundia, nicknamed
      <i>
       The Lady
      </i>
      . In the late 19th century, several other railroads connected the interior to the state capital. So Paulo became the point of convergence of all railroads from the interior of the state. Coffee was the economic engine for major economic and population growth in the State of So Paulo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1888, the "Golden Law" (
      <i>
       Lei urea
      </i>
      ) was sanctioned by
      <a href="/wiki/Isabel,_Princess_Imperial_of_Brazil" title="Isabel, Princess Imperial of Brazil">
       Isabel, Princess Imperial of Brazil
      </a>
      , declaring abolished the slavery institution in Brazil. Slaves were the main source of labour in the coffee plantations until then. As a consequence of this law, and following governmental stimulus towards the increase of immigration, the province began to receive a large number of immigrants, largely Italians, Japanese and Portuguese peasants, many of whom settled in the capital. The region's first industries also began to emerge, providing jobs to the newcomers, especially those who had to learn Portuguese.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Republican_Period">
       Old Republican Period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Old Republican Period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="709" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg/220px-Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg/330px-Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg/440px-Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Paulista_1902.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">
         Paulista Avenue
        </a>
        in 1902.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      By the time Brazil became a republic in November 15, 1889, coffee exports were still an important part of So Paulo's economy. So Paulo grew strong in the national political scene, taking turns with the also rich state of Minas Gerais in electing Brazilian presidents, an alliance that became known as "
      <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_com_leite_politics" title="Caf com leite politics">
       coffee and milk
      </a>
      ", given that Minas Gerais was famous for its dairy produce.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Industrialization was the economic cycle that followed the coffee plantation model. By the hands of some industrious families, including many immigrants of Italian and Jewish origin, factories began to arise and So Paulo became known for its smoky, foggy air. The cultural scene followed
      <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">
       modernist
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Naturalism_(philosophy)" title="Naturalism (philosophy)">
       naturalist
      </a>
      tendencies in fashion at the beginning of the 20th century. Some examples of notable modernist artists are poets
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade" title="Mrio de Andrade">
       Mrio de Andrade
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Oswald_de_Andrade" title="Oswald de Andrade">
       Oswald de Andrade
      </a>
      , artists
      <a href="/wiki/Anita_Malfatti" title="Anita Malfatti">
       Anita Malfatti
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tarsila_do_Amaral" title="Tarsila do Amaral">
       Tarsila do Amaral
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lasar_Segall" title="Lasar Segall">
       Lasar Segall
      </a>
      , and sculptor
      <a href="/wiki/Victor_Brecheret" title="Victor Brecheret">
       Victor Brecheret
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Modern_Art_Week" title="Modern Art Week">
       Modern Art Week
      </a>
      of 1922 that took place at the
      <a href="/wiki/Theatro_Municipal_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Theatro Municipal (So Paulo)">
       Theatro Municipal
      </a>
      was an event marked by
      <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">
       avant-garde
      </a>
      ideas and works of art.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      So Paulo's main economic activities derive from the services industryfactories are since long gone, and in came financial services institutions, law firms, consulting firms. Old factory buildings and warehouses still dot the landscape in neighborhoods such as
      <a href="/wiki/Barra_Funda" title="Barra Funda">
       Barra Funda
      </a>
      and Brs. Some cities around So Paulo, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Diadema,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Diadema, So Paulo">
       Diadema
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Bernardo_do_Campo" title="So Bernardo do Campo">
       So Bernardo do Campo
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Andr%C3%A9" title="Santo Andr">
       Santo Andr
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Cubat%C3%A3o" title="Cubato">
       Cubato
      </a>
      are still heavily industrialized to the present day, with factories producing from cosmetics to chemicals to automobiles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutionalist_Revolution_of_1932">
       Constitutionalist Revolution of 1932
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Constitutionalist Revolution of 1932">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2485" data-file-width="3589" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg/220px-Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg/330px-Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg/440px-Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Obelisco_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Brasil.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Obelisk_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Obelisk of So Paulo">
         Obelisk of So Paulo
        </a>
        , a symbol of the
        <a href="/wiki/Constitutionalist_Revolution" title="Constitutionalist Revolution">
         Constitutionalist Revolution
        </a>
        of 1932
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      This "revolution" is considered by some historians as the last armed conflict to take place in Brazil's history. In July 9, 1932, the population of So Paulo town rose against a
      <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'tat">
       coup d'tat
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas" title="Getlio Vargas">
       Getlio Vargas
      </a>
      to take the presidential office. The movement grew out of local resentment from the fact that Vargas ruled by decree, unbound by a constitution, in a provisional government. The 1930 coup also affected So Paulo by eroding the autonomy that states enjoyed during the term of the 1891 Constitution and preventing the inauguration of the governor of So Paulo Jlio Prestes in the Presidency of the Republic, while simultaneously overthrowing President
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Lu%C3%ADs" title="Washington Lus">
       Washington Lus
      </a>
      , who was governor of So Paulo from 1920 to 1924. These events marked the end of the Old Republic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The uprising commenced on July 9, 1932, after four protesting students were killed by federal government troops on May 23, 1932. On the wake of their deaths, a movement called MMDC (from the initials of the names of each of the four students killed, Martins, Miragaia, Drusio and Camargo) started. A fifth victim, Alvarenga, was also shot that night, but died months later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a few months, the state of So Paulo rebelled against the federal government. Counting on the solidarity of the political elites of two other powerful states, (
      <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">
       Minas Gerais
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">
       Rio Grande do Sul
      </a>
      ), the politicians from So Paulo expected a quick war. However, that solidarity was never translated into actual support, and the So Paulo revolt was militarily crushed on October 2, 1932. In total, there were 87 days of fighting (July 9 to October 4, 1932with the last two days after the surrender of So Paulo), with a balance of 934 official deaths, though non-official estimates report up to 2,200 dead, and many cities in the state of So Paulo suffered damage due to fighting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There is an obelisk in front of
      <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">
       Ibirapuera Park
      </a>
      that serves as a memorial to the young men that died for the MMDC. The
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of So Paulo">
       University of So Paulo
      </a>
      's Law School also pays homage to the students that died during this period with plaques hung on its arcades.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br_8-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-sasopaulo.blogspot.com.br-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
       Geography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_setting">
       Physical setting
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Physical setting">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2520" data-file-width="3776" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG/220px-Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG/330px-Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG/440px-Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pico_do_jaragua_aerial_2010.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1" title="Pico do Jaragu">
         Jaragu Peak
        </a>
        is the highest point in the city, at 1,135 metres (3,724ft).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
         <a href="#cite_note-9">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          9
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo is located in
      <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Southeast Region, Brazil">
       Southeastern Brazil
      </a>
      , in southeastern So Paulo State, approximately halfway between
      <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">
       Curitiba
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
       Rio de Janeiro
      </a>
      . The city is located on a
      <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">
       plateau
      </a>
      located beyond the
      <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">
       Serra do Mar
      </a>
      (Portuguese for "Sea Range" or "Coastal Range"), itself a component of the vast region known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Highlands" title="Brazilian Highlands">
       Brazilian Highlands
      </a>
      , with an average elevation of around 799 metres (2,621ft)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
       above sea level
      </a>
      , although being at a distance of only about 70 kilometres (43mi) from
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
       the Atlantic Ocean
      </a>
      . The distance is covered by two highways, the
      <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Anchieta" title="Rodovia Anchieta">
       Anchieta
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Imigrantes" title="Rodovia dos Imigrantes">
       Imigrantes
      </a>
      , (see "
      <a href="#Transportation">
       Transportation
      </a>
      " below) that roll down the range, leading to the port city of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santos,_Brazil" title="Santos, Brazil">
       Santos
      </a>
      and the beach resort of
      <a href="/wiki/Guaruj%C3%A1" title="Guaruj">
       Guaruj
      </a>
      . Rolling terrain prevails within the urbanized areas of So Paulo except in its northern area, where the
      <a href="/wiki/Serra_da_Cantareira" title="Serra da Cantareira">
       Serra da Cantareira
      </a>
      Range reaches a higher elevation and a sizable remnant of the
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Forest" title="Atlantic Forest">
       Atlantic Rain Forest
      </a>
      . The region is seismically stable and no significant
      <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">
       seismic activity
      </a>
      has ever been recorded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_area">
       Metropolitan area
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Metropolitan area">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater So Paulo">
       Greater So Paulo
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1447" data-file-width="1062" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg/220px-Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg/330px-Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg/440px-Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_at_night.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Satellite view of
        <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater So Paulo">
         Greater So Paulo
        </a>
        at night.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The nonspecific term "Grande So Paulo" ("
      <i>
       Greater So Paulo
      </i>
      ") covers multiple definitions. The legally defined
      <i>
       Regio Metropolitana de So Paulo
      </i>
      consists of 39 municipalities in total and a population of 21,1 milliion
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bra_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bra-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      inhabitants (as of 2014 National Census).
     </p>
     <p>
      Because So Paulo has significant
      <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">
       urban sprawl
      </a>
      , it uses a different definition for its metropolitan area called
      <a href="/wiki/Expanded_Metropolitan_Complex_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Expanded Metropolitan Complex of So Paulo">
       Expanded Metropolitan Complex of So Paulo
      </a>
      . Analogous to the
      <a href="/wiki/BosWash" title="BosWash">
       BosWash
      </a>
      definition, it is one of the largest urban aglomerations in the world, with 32 million inhabitants,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      behind
      <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">
       Tokyo
      </a>
      , which includes 4 contiguous legally defined metropolitan regions and 3 microregions.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">
       Hydrography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hydrography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Water_management_in_the_Metropolitan_Region_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Water management in the Metropolitan Region of So Paulo">
       Water management in the Metropolitan Region of So Paulo
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tiet River">
       Tiet River
      </a>
      and its
      <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">
       tributary
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Pinheiros_River" title="Pinheiros River">
       Pinheiros River
      </a>
      , were once important sources of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">
       fresh water
      </a>
      and leisure for So Paulo. However, heavy industrial
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effluents" title="Effluents">
       effluents
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Wastewater" title="Wastewater">
       wastewater
      </a>
      discharges in the later 20th century caused the rivers to become heavily
      <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">
       polluted
      </a>
      . A substantial clean-up program for both rivers is underway, financed through a partnership between local government and
      <a href="/wiki/International_development" title="International development">
       international development
      </a>
      banks such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Bank_for_International_Cooperation" title="Japan Bank for International Cooperation">
       Japan Bank for International Cooperation
      </a>
      . Neither river is navigable in the stretch that flows through the city, although
      <a href="/wiki/Water_transportation" title="Water transportation">
       water transportation
      </a>
      becomes increasingly important on the Tiet river further downstream (near
      <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paran River">
       river Paran
      </a>
      ), as the river is part of the
      <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Ro de la Plata">
       River Plate
      </a>
      basin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      No large natural lakes exist in the region, but the
      <a href="/wiki/Billings_Reservoir" title="Billings Reservoir">
       Billings
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Guarapiranga" title="Guarapiranga">
       Guarapiranga
      </a>
      reservoirs in the city's southern outskirts are used for
      <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">
       power generation
      </a>
      , water storage and leisure activities, such as sailing. The original
      <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">
       flora
      </a>
      consisted mainly of
      <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">
       broadleaf
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">
       evergreens
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">
       non-native species
      </a>
      are common, as the mild climate and abundant rainfall permit a multitude of tropical, subtropical and temperate plants to be cultivated, especially the ubiquitous
      <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">
       eucalyptus
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2015, So Paulo experienced a
      <a href="/wiki/2015_Brazilian_drought" title="2015 Brazilian drought">
       major drought
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt2.2015_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nyt2.2015-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
       Climate
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The city has a monsoon-influenced
      <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">
       humid subtropical climate
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Cfa/Cwa
      </i>
      ), according to the
      <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Kppen climate classification">
       Kppen classification
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In summer (January through March), the mean low temperature is about 17C (63F) and the mean high temperatures is near 28C (82F). In winter, temperatures tend to range between 11 and 23C (52 and 73F).
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tempestade_em_SP.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2144" data-file-width="3216" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tempestade_em_SP.jpg/220px-Tempestade_em_SP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tempestade_em_SP.jpg/330px-Tempestade_em_SP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tempestade_em_SP.jpg/440px-Tempestade_em_SP.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tempestade_em_SP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Heavy rain and lightning in So Paulo, which has the largest number of
        <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">
         lightning
        </a>
        incidents amongst Brazilian state capitals.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
         <a href="#cite_note-17">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          17
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The recorded high was 37.8C (100.0F) on October 17, 2014
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the lowest 2C (28F) on August 2, 1955 and on the same day 3.8C (25.2F) was recorded unofficially. Temperature averages are similar to those of
      <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">
       Sydney
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">
       Tropic of Capricorn
      </a>
      , at about 2327' S, passes through north of So Paulo and roughly marks the boundary between the tropical and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">
       temperate
      </a>
      areas of South America. Because of its elevation, however, So Paulo enjoys a temperate climate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The city experiences relatively four distinct seasons. The winter is mild and sub-dry, and the summer is moderately warm and rainy. Fall and spring are transitional seasons.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frosts" title="Frosts">
       Frosts
      </a>
      occur sporadically in regions further away from the center, in some winters throughout the city. Regions further away from the center and in cities in the metropolitan area, can reach temperatures next to 0C (32F), or even lower in the winter.
     </p>
     <p>
      Rainfall is abundant, annually averaging 1,454 millimetres (57.2in).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is especially common in the warmer months averaging 219 millimetres (8.6in) and decreases in winter, averaging 47 millimetres (1.9in). Neither So Paulo nor the nearby coast has ever been hit by a
      <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">
       tropical cyclone
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">
       tornadic
      </a>
      activity is uncommon. During late winter, especially August, the city experiences the phenomenon known as
      <i>
       "veranico"
      </i>
      or
      <i>
       "verozinho"
      </i>
      ("little summer"), which consists of hot and dry weather, sometimes reaching temperatures well above 28C (82F). On the other hand, relatively cool days during summer are fairly common when persistent winds blow from the ocean. On such occasions daily high temperatures may not surpass 20C (68F), accompanied by lows often below 15C (59F), however, summer can be extremely hot when a heat wave hits the city followed by temperatures around 34C (93F), but in places with greater skyscraper density and less tree cover, the temperature can feel like 39C (102F), as on
      <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">
       Paulista Avenue
      </a>
      for example. In the summer of 2012, So Paulo was affected by a heat wave that lasted for 2 weeks with highs going from 29 to 34C (84 to 93F) on the hottest days. Secondary to
      <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
       deforestation
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Groundwater_pollution" title="Groundwater pollution">
       groundwater pollution
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">
       climate change
      </a>
      , So Paulo is increasingly susceptible to
      <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">
       drought
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_shortage" title="Water shortage">
       water shortages
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Due to the altitude of the city, there are few hot nights in So Paulo even in the summer months, with minimum temperatures rarely exceeding 21C (69F). In winter, however, the strong inflow of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_fronts" title="Cold fronts">
       cold fronts
      </a>
      accompanied by excessive cloudiness and polar air cause very low temperatures, even in the afternoon.
     </p>
     <p>
      Afternoons with maximum temperatures ranging between 13C (55F) and 15C (59F) are common even during the fall and early spring. During the winter, there have been several recent records of cold afternoons, as on July 24, 2013 in which the maximum temperature was 8C (46F) and the
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_chill" title="Wind chill">
       wind chill
      </a>
      hit 0C (32F) during all afternoon.
     </p>
     <p>
      So Paulo is also known for its rapidly changing weather. Locals say that all four seasons can be experienced in one day. In the morning, when winds blow from the ocean, the weather can be cool or sometimes even cold. When the sun hits its peak, the weather can be extremely dry and hot. When the sun sets, the cold wind comes back bringing cool temperatures. This phenomenon happens usually in the winter.
     </p>
     <p>
      <br/>
     </p>
