     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demographics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Demographics of So Paulo">
       Demographics of So Paulo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brazil" title="Demographics of Brazil">
       Demographics of Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="barbox tleft" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:287px; background: white;">
      <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
       <tr style="background:#ddd">
        <th colspan="5">
         Race and ethnicity in So Paulo
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
        <td style="padding:0 4px;">
         Ethnicity
        </td>
        <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
        </td>
        <td style="width:100px;">
        </td>
        <td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">
         Percentage
        </td>
        <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" title="White Brazilian">
          White
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:Blue; width:60.6%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         60.6%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">
          Pardo
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Multiracial#Brazil" title="Multiracial">
          Multiracial
         </a>
         )
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:green; width:30.5%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         30.5%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Brazilian" title="Black Brazilian">
          Black
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:Black; width:6.5%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         6.5%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" title="Asian Brazilian">
          Asian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:red; width:2.2%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         2.2%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">
          Amerindian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:yellow; width:0.2%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         0.2%
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2013, So Paulo was the most populous city in Brazil and in South America.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">
       2010 IBGE Census
      </a>
      , there were 11,244,369 people residing in the city of So Paulo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The census found 6,824,668
      <a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" title="White Brazilian">
       White
      </a>
      people (60.6%), 3,433,218
      <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">
       Pardo
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Multiracial#Brazil" title="Multiracial">
       multiracial
      </a>
      ) people (30.5%), 736,083
      <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" title="Afro-Brazilian">
       Black
      </a>
      people (6.5%), 246,244
      <a href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" title="Asian Brazilian">
       Asian
      </a>
      people (2.2%) and 21,318
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">
       Amerindian
      </a>
      people (0.2%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censo2010.ibge.gov.br_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-censo2010.ibge.gov.br-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2010, the city had 2,146,077 opposite-sex couples and 7,532
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same-sex_couple" title="Same-sex couple">
       same-sex couples
      </a>
      . The population of So Paulo was 52.6% female and 47.4% male.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censo2010.ibge.gov.br_33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-censo2010.ibge.gov.br-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">
       Immigration
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Immigration">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">
       Immigration to Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1072" data-file-width="2055" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg/220px-Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg/330px-Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg/440px-Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Italians_Sao_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" title="Italian Brazilian">
         Italian
        </a>
        immigrants arriving in the city. Brazil has the largest Italian population outside Italy, with So Paulo being the most populous city with Italian ancestry in the world.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
         <a href="#cite_note-34">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          34
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bazar_syrien,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_1950.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="272" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Bazar_syrien%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_1950.jpg/220px-Bazar_syrien%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_1950.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Bazar_syrien%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_1950.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Bazar_syrien%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_1950.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bazar_syrien,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_1950.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilian" title="Arab Brazilian">
         Arab
        </a>
        immigrants in the city of So Paulo, 1940s.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="602" data-file-width="436" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg/220px-Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg/330px-Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liberdade_sao_paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberdade" title="Liberdade">
         Liberdade
        </a>
        district is a
        <a href="/wiki/Japantown" title="Japantown">
         Japantown
        </a>
        of So Paulo.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo is considered the most
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicultural" title="Multicultural">
       multicultural
      </a>
      city in
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      and one of the most diverse in the world. Since 1870 to 2010, approximately 2.3 million
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">
       immigrants
      </a>
      arrived in the state, from all parts of the world. Currently, it is the city with the largest populations of ethnic
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">
       Italian
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" title="Japanese Brazilian">
       Japanese
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
       Spanish
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">
       Lebanese
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
       Arab
      </a>
      outside of their respective countries.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Italian community is one of the strongest, with a presence throughout the city. Of the ten million inhabitants of So Paulo, 60% (six million people) have some Italian ancestry. So Paulo has more descendants of Italians than any other Italian city (the largest city of
      <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
       Italy
      </a>
      is
      <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
       Rome
      </a>
      , with 2.5 million inhabitants). Even today, Italians are grouped in neighborhoods like Bixiga, Bras and
      <a href="/wiki/Mooca_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Mooca (district of So Paulo)">
       Mooca
      </a>
      to promote celebrations and festivals. In the early twentieth century, the Italian and the dialects were spoken as much as the
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      in the city, which influenced the formation of the So Paulo dialect of today. So Paulo is the second largest consumer of
      <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">
       pizza
      </a>
      in the world.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Six thousand pizzerias are producing about a million pizzas a day.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Portuguese community is also quite large, and it is estimated that three million paulistanos have some origin in
      <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
       Portugal
      </a>
      . The Jewish colony is more than 60,000 people in So Paulo and is concentrated mainly in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higien%C3%B3polis,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Higienpolis, So Paulo">
       Higienpolis
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bom_Retiro_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Bom Retiro (district of So Paulo)">
       Bom Retiro
      </a>
      . From the nineteenth century through the first half of the twentieth century, So Paulo also received
      <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">
       German
      </a>
      immigrants (in the current neighborhood of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Amaro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santo Amaro, So Paulo">
       Santo Amaro
      </a>
      ),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
       Spanish
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" title="Lithuanian people">
       Lithuanian
      </a>
      (in the neighborhood Vila Zelina).
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable sortable">
      <caption>
       So Paulo City in 1886
      </caption>
      <tr>
       <th>
        Immigrants
       </th>
       <th>
        Percentage of immigrants in foreign born population
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
         <a href="#cite_note-35">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          35
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
         Italians
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        47.9%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
         Portuguese
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        29.3%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">
         Germans
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        9.9%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">
         Spaniards
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        3.2%
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      <i>
       A French observer, travelling to So Paulo at the time, noted that there was a division of the capitalist class, by nationality (...) Germans, French and Italians shared the dry goods sector with Brazilians. Foodstuffs was generally the province of either Portuguese or Brazilians, except for bakery and pastry which was the domain of the French and Germans. Shoes and tinware were mostly controlled by Italians. However, the larger metallurgical plants were in the hands of the English and the Americans. (...) Italians outnumbered Brazilians two to one in So Paulo.
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Until 1920, 1,078,437
      <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
       Italians
      </a>
      entered in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="State of So Paulo">
       State of So Paulo
      </a>
      . Of the immigrants who arrived there between 1887 and 1902, 63.5% came from Italy. Between 1888 and 1919, 44.7% of the immigrants were Italians, 19.2% were
      <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">
       Spaniards
      </a>
      and 15.4% were
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1920, nearly 80% of So Paulo city's population was composed of immigrants and their descendants and Italians made up over half of its male population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o_37-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At that time, the Governor of So Paulo said that
      <i>
       "if the owner of each house in So Paulo display the flag of the country of origin on the roof, from above So Paulo would look like an Italian city".
      </i>
      In 1900, a columnist who was absent from So Paulo for 20 years wrote
      <i>
       "then So Paulo used to be a genuine Paulista city, today it is an Italian city."
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o_37-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable sortable">
      <caption>
       So Paulo City
      </caption>
      <tr>

        Year
       </th>

       </th>

        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigra.C3.A7.C3.A3o_37-3">

          <span>
           [
          </span>

          <span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        1886
       </td>
       <td>
        5,717
       </td>
       <td>
        13%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        1893
       </td>
       <td>
        45,457
       </td>
       <td>
        35%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        1900
       </td>
       <td>

       </td>

       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

       </td>

       </td>

       </td>
      </tr>

       </td>

       </td>

        37%
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Research conducted by the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of So Paulo">
       University of So Paulo
      </a>
      (USP) shows the city's high ethnic diversity: when asked if they are "descendants of foreign immigrants", 81% of the students reported "yes". The main reported ancestries were: Italian (30.5%), Portuguese (23%), Spanish (14%), Japanese (8%), German (5.6%),
      <i>
       Brazilian
      </i>
      (4.3%), African (2.8%), Arab (2.4%) and Jewish (1.2%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_migration">
       Domestic migration
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Domestic migration">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Since the 19th century people began migrating from Northeastern Brazil into So Paulo. This migration grew enormously in the 1930s and remained huge in the next decades. The concentration of land, modernization in rural areas, changes in work relationships and cycles of droughts stimulated migration. Northeastern migrants live mainly in hazardous and unhealthy areas of the city, in
      <a href="/wiki/Corti%C3%A7o" title="Cortio">
       cortios
      </a>
      , in various slums (
      <a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">
       favelas
      </a>
      ) of the metropolis, because they offer cheaper housing. The largest concentration of Northeastern migrants was found in the area of S/Brs (districts of Brs,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bom_Retiro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Bom Retiro, So Paulo">
       Bom Retiro
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cambuci" title="Cambuci">
       Cambuci
      </a>
      , Pari and
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="S (district of So Paulo)">
       S
      </a>
      ). In this area they composed 41% of the population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1708px;">
      <div class="thumbinner">
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazil_-_SP.jpg" title="Panoramic view of Central Zone of So Paulo from Altino Arantes Building.">
         <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="4174" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Brazil_-_SP.jpg/1700px-Brazil_-_SP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Brazil_-_SP.jpg/2550px-Brazil_-_SP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Brazil_-_SP.jpg/3400px-Brazil_-_SP.jpg 2x" width="1700"/>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Brazil_-_SP.jpg" title="File:Brazil - SP.jpg">
         </a>
        </div>
        Panoramic view of
        <a href="/wiki/Central_Zone_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Central Zone of So Paulo">
         Central Zone of So Paulo
        </a>
        from
        <a href="/wiki/Altino_Arantes_Building" title="Altino Arantes Building">
         Altino Arantes Building
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      As in all of Brazil, people of different ethnicities mix with each other, producing a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiethnic_society" title="Multiethnic society">
       multi-ethnic
      </a>
      society. Today, people of many different
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">
       ethnicities
      </a>
      make So Paulo their home.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The main groups, considering all the metropolitan area, are: 6 million people of Italian descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      3 million people of Portuguese descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1.7million people of African descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1 million people of Arab descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      665,000 people of Japanese descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_44-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      400,000 people of German descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_44-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      250,000 people of
      <a href="/wiki/French_Brazilian" title="French Brazilian">
       French descent
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_44-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      150,000 people of
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_Brazilian" title="Greek Brazilian">
       Greek descent
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_44-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      120,000 people of Chinese descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_44-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      120,000-300,000
      <a href="/wiki/Bolivians_in_Brazil" title="Bolivians in Brazil">
       Bolivian immigrants
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      50,000 people of Korean descent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 40,000 Jews.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo is also receiving waves of immigration from Haiti and from many countries of Africa. Those immigrants are mainly concentrated in Praca da S, Glicrio and Vale do Anhangaba [central zone of the city]. Haitians are already a significant group in the city. African immigrants are also a growing group in the city and metropolitan area.
     </p>
     <div class="center">
      <p>
       <b>
        Changing demographics of the city of So Paulo
       </b>

      </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
       Religion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catedral_da_S%C3%A9_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
       Languages
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Languages">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Brazil" title="Languages of Brazil">
       Languages of Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MLP.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/MLP.jpg/220px-MLP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/MLP.jpg/330px-MLP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/MLP.jpg/440px-MLP.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MLP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">
         Museum of the Portuguese Language
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The primary language is
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The general language from So Paulo General, or
      <a href="/wiki/Tupi_language" title="Tupi language">
       Tupi Austral
      </a>
      (Southern Tupi), was the Tupi-based trade language of what is now So Vicente, So Paulo, and the upper Tiet River. In the 17th century it was widely spoken in So Paulo and spread to neighboring regions. From 1750 on, following orders from
      <a href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Pombal" title="Marquess of Pombal">
       Marquess of Pombal
      </a>
      , Portuguese language was introduced through immigration and consequently taught to children in schools. The original
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupi_Austral" title="Tupi Austral">
       Tupi Austral
      </a>
      language subsequently lost ground to
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      , and eventually became extinct.
     </p>
     <p>
      Due to the large influx of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilians" title="Japanese Brazilians">
       Japanese
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Brazilians" title="German Brazilians">
       German
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilians_of_Spanish_descent" title="Brazilians of Spanish descent">
       Spanish
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" title="Italian Brazilian">
       Italian
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilian" title="Arab Brazilian">
       Arab
      </a>
      immigrants &amp; etc., the Portuguese idiom spoken in the metropolitan area of So Paulo reflects some significant influences from those languages.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Italian influence in So Paulo accents is evident in the traditional Italian neighborhoods such as Bela Vista, Moca, Brs and Lapa. Italian mingled with Portuguese and as an old influence, was assimilated or disappeared into spoken language. The local accent with Italian influences became notorious through the songs of
      <a href="/wiki/Adoniran_Barbosa" title="Adoniran Barbosa">
       Adoniran Barbosa
      </a>
      , a Brazilian
      <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">
       samba
      </a>
      singer born to Italian parents who used to sing using the local accent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Other languages spoken in the city are mainly among the Asian community: the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberdade" title="Liberdade">
       Liberdade
      </a>
      neighborhood is home to the largest Japanese population outside of Japan. Although today most Japanese-Brazilians speak only Portuguese, some of them are still fluent in Japanese. Some people of Chinese and Korean descent are still able to speak their ancestral languages.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In some areas it is still possible to find descendants of immigrants who speak German
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (especially in the area of Brooklin paulista) and Russian or East European languages (especially in the area of Vila Zelina).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the west zone of So Paulo, specially at Vila Anastcio and Lapa region, there is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">
       Hungarian
      </a>
      colony, with three churches (Calvinist, Baptist and Catholic), so on Sundays it is possible to see Hungarians talking to each other on sidewalks.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_challenges">
       Social challenges
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Social challenges">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Favela_Jaqueline_(Vila_S%C3%B4nia)_01.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Favela_Jaqueline_%28Vila_S%C3%B4nia%29_01.jpg/220px-Favela_Jaqueline_%28Vila_S%C3%B4nia%29_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Favela_Jaqueline_%28Vila_S%C3%B4nia%29_01.jpg/330px-Favela_Jaqueline_%28Vila_S%C3%B4nia%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Favela_Jaqueline_%28Vila_S%C3%B4nia%29_01.jpg/440px-Favela_Jaqueline_%28Vila_S%C3%B4nia%29_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Favela_Jaqueline_(Vila_S%C3%B4nia)_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">
         Slum
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">
          favela
         </a>
        </i>
        ) in So Paulo.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Social_issues_in_Brazil" title="Social issues in Brazil">
       Social issues in Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since the beginning of the 20th century, So Paulo has been a major economic center in Latin America. During two
      <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">
       World Wars
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      , coffee exports (from other regions of the state) were critically affected. This led wealthy coffee farmers to invest in industrial activities that turned So Paulo into Brazil's largest industrial hub.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_statistics" title="Crime statistics">
        Crime rates
       </a>
       consistently decreased in the 21st century. The city-wide homicide rate was 9.0 in 2011, less than half the 22.3 national rate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         54
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Air quality
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         55
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       has steadily increased during the modern era.
      </li>
      <li>
       The two major rivers crossing the city,
       <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tiet River">
        Tiet
       </a>
       and Pinheiros, are highly polluted. A major project to clean up these rivers is underway.
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cidade_Limpa" title="Cidade Limpa">
        Clean City Law
       </a>
       or anti
       <a href="/wiki/Billboard" title="Billboard">
        billboard
       </a>
       , approved in 2007, focused on two main targets: antipublicity and anticommerce. Advertisers estimate that they removed 15,000 billboards and that more than 1,600
       <a href="/wiki/Signage" title="Signage">
        signs
       </a>
       and 1,300 towering metal panels were dismantled by authorities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         56
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       So Paulo metropolitan region, adopted vehicle restrictions from 1996 to 1998 to reduce air pollution during wintertime. Since 1997, a similar project was implemented throughout the year in the central area of So Paulo to improve traffic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         57
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>

           <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">
            Moscow
           </a>
          </b>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
           Russia
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="flagicon">
           <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
            <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
            New York City
           </a>
          </b>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           United States
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="flagicon">
           <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
            <img alt="France" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
            Paris
           </a>
          </b>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
           France
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1918" data-file-width="3612" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/220px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/330px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/440px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">
         So Paulo Stock Exchange
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paulista_at_night.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Paulista_at_night.jpg/220px-Paulista_at_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Paulista_at_night.jpg/330px-Paulista_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Paulista_at_night.jpg/440px-Paulista_at_night.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paulista_at_night.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">
         Paulista Avenue
        </a>
        at night.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ponte_e_rio.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2301" data-file-width="3626" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ponte_e_rio.jpg/220px-Ponte_e_rio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ponte_e_rio.jpg/330px-Ponte_e_rio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ponte_e_rio.jpg/440px-Ponte_e_rio.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ponte_e_rio.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Commercial buildings in
        <a href="/wiki/Brooklin_Novo" title="Brooklin Novo">
         Brooklin Novo
        </a>
        , featured the
        <a href="/wiki/Oct%C3%A1vio_Frias_de_Oliveira_Bridge" title="Octvio Frias de Oliveira Bridge">
         Octvio Frias de Oliveira Bridge
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Centro_Empresarial_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_Unidas" title="Centro Empresarial Naes Unidas">
         Centro Empresarial Naes Unidas
        </a>
        (background).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1680" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/220px-Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/330px-Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/440px-Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        So Paulo at night.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Economy of So Paulo">
       Economy of So Paulo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">
       Economy of Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo is considered the "financial capital of Brazil", as it is the location for the headquarters of many major corporations and the country's most renowned banks and financial institutions. So Paulo is
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">
       Brazil's highest GDP city
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">
       10th largest in the world
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Estad.C3.A3o_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Estad.C3.A3o-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      using
      <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">
       Purchasing power parity
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to data of
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">
       IBGE
      </a>
      , its gross domestic product (GDP) in 2010 was R$450 billion,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      approximately
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$220
      </span>
      billion, 12.26% of Brazilian GDP and 36% of all production of
      <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_services" title="Goods and services">
       goods and services
      </a>
      of the State of So Paulo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">
       PricewaterhouseCoopers
      </a>
      average annual economic growth of the city is 4.2%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo also has a large "informal" economy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005, the city of So Paulo collected R$90billion in taxes and the city budget was R$15billion. The city has 1,500 bank
      <a href="/wiki/Branch" title="Branch">
       branches
      </a>
      and 70 shopping malls.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2014, So Paulo is the third largest exporting municipality in Brazil after
      <a href="/wiki/Parauapebas" title="Parauapebas">
       Parauapebas, PA
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
       Rio de Janeiro, RJ
      </a>
      . In that year So Paulo's exported goods totaled $7.32B (USD) or 3.02% of Brazil's total exports. The top five material goods exported by So Paulo are
      <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">
       Soybean
      </a>
      (21%),
      <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">
       Raw Sugar
      </a>
      (19%),
      <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
       Coffee
      </a>
      (6.5%),
      <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(paper)" title="Pulp (paper)">
       Sulfate Chemical Wood Pulp
      </a>
      (5.6%), and
      <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">
       Corn
      </a>
      (4.4%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">
       So Paulo Stock Exchange
      </a>
      (BM&amp;F Bovespa) is Brazil's official stock and bond exchange. It is the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">
       stock exchange
      </a>
      in Latin America, trading about R$6billion (US$3.5billion) every day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo's economy is going through a deep transformation. Once a city with a strong
      <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">
       industrial character
      </a>
      , So Paulo's economy has followed the global trend of shifting to the
      <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">
       tertiary sector of the economy
      </a>
      , focusing on services. The city is unique among Brazilian cities for its large number of foreign corporations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      63% of all the
      <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">
       international companies
      </a>
      with business in Brazil have their head offices in So Paulo. So Paulo has the largest concentration of German businesses worldwide
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is the largest Swedish industrial hub alongside Gothenburg.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo ranked second after New York in
      <a href="/wiki/FDi_magazine" title="FDi magazine">
       FDi magazine
      </a>
      's bi-annual ranking of Cities of the Future 2013/14 in the
      <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
       Americas
      </a>
      , and was named the Latin American City of the Future 2013/14, overtaking
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Chile" title="Santiago de Chile">
       Santiago de Chile
      </a>
      , the first city in the previous ranking. Santiago now ranks second, followed by
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
       Rio de Janeiro
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The per capita income for the city was R$32,493 in 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">
       Mercer
      </a>
      's 2011
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees#Mercer_surveys" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">
       city rankings of cost of living for expatriate employees
      </a>
      , So Paulo is now among the ten most expensive cities in the world, ranking 10th in 2011, up from 21st in 2010 and ahead of
      <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
       London
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
       Paris
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">
       Milan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York City
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">
       Science and technology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Science and technology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="907" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg/220px-Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg/330px-Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg/440px-Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Rua_Oscar_Freire" title="Rua Oscar Freire">
         Oscar Freire Street
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Jardins" title="Jardins">
         Jardins
        </a>
        neighbourhood, voted the eighth most luxurious street in the World.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
         <a href="#cite_note-82">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          82
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_science_and_technology" title="Brazilian science and technology">
       Brazilian science and technology
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The city of So Paulo is home to research and development facilities and attracts companies due to the presence of several regionally renowned universities. Science, technology and innovation is leveraged by the allocation of funds from the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="So Paulo (state)">
       state government
      </a>
      , mainly carried out by means of the Foundation to Research Support in the State of So Paulo (Fundao de Amparo  Pesquisa do Estado de So Paulo FAPESP), one of the main agencies promoting scientific and technological research.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Luxury_goods">
       Luxury goods
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Luxury goods">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luxury_brand" title="Luxury brand">
       Luxury brands
      </a>
      tend to concentrate their business in So Paulo . So Paulo, the most important city in the country is the main place for them to start opening their business. Because of the lack of department stores and multi-brand boutiques,
      <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">
       shopping malls
      </a>
      as well as the
      <a href="/wiki/Jardins" title="Jardins">
       Jardins
      </a>
      district, which is more or less the Brazilian's
      <a href="/wiki/Rodeo_Drive" title="Rodeo Drive">
       Rodeo Drive
      </a>
      version, attract most of the world's luxurious brands.
     </p>
     <p>
      Most of the international luxury brands can be found in the
      <a href="/wiki/Iguatemi_Empresa_de_Shopping_Centers" title="Iguatemi Empresa de Shopping Centers">
       Iguatemi
      </a>
      , Cidade Jardim or JK shopping malls or on the streets of
      <a href="/wiki/Rua_Oscar_Freire" title="Rua Oscar Freire">
       Oscar Freire
      </a>
      , Lorena or Haddock Lobo in the Jardins district. They are home of brands such as
      <a href="/wiki/Cartier_(jeweler)" title="Cartier (jeweler)">
       Cartier
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">
       Chanel
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dior" title="Dior">
       Dior
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Armani" title="Giorgio Armani">
       Giorgio Armani
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">
       Gucci
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">
       Louis Vuitton
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">
       Marc Jacobs
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co" title="Tiffany &amp; Co">
       Tiffany &amp; Co
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Cidade Jardim was opened in So Paulo in 2008, it is a 45,000 square meters mall, landscaped with trees and greenery scenario, with a focus on Brazilian brands but also home to international luxury brands such as
      <a href="/wiki/Herm%C3%A8s" title="Herms">
       Herms
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Choo" title="Jimmy Choo">
       Jimmy Choo
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pucci" title="Pucci">
       Pucci
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Herrera_(fashion_designer)" title="Carolina Herrera (fashion designer)">
       Carolina Herrera
      </a>
      . Opened in 2012, JK shopping mall has brought to Brazil brands that were not present in the country before such as, Goyard, Tory Burch, Llc.,
      <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">
       Prada
      </a>
      , and Miu Miu.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Iguatemi_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Iguatemi So Paulo">
       Iguatemi
      </a>
      Faria Lima, in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avenida_Brigadeiro_Faria_Lima" title="Avenida Brigadeiro Faria Lima">
       Faria Lima Avenue
      </a>
      , is Brazil's oldest mall, opened in 1966.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Jardins" title="Jardins">
       Jardins
      </a>
      neighborhood is regarded among the most sophisticated places in town, with upscale restaurants and hotels. The New York Times once compared Oscar Freire Street to
      <a href="/wiki/Rodeo_Drive" title="Rodeo Drive">
       Rodeo Drive
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Jardins there are luxury car dealers. One of the world's best restaurants as elected by The World's 50 Best Restaurants Award, D.O.M.,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is located there.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
       Tourism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tourism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brazil" title="Tourism in Brazil">
       Tourism in Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1496" data-file-width="2256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG/220px-Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG/330px-Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG/440px-Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Municipal Market of Sao Paulo
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera,_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_(biennale)_07.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG/220px-Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG/330px-Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG/440px-Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera,_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_(biennale)_07.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="So Paulo Art Biennial">
         So Paulo Art Biennial
        </a>
        . The second oldest art biennial in the world after the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venice_Biennial" title="Venice Biennial">
         Venice Biennial
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo stands out more as a city marked by the business tourism that the recreational tourism. Large hotel chains whose target audience is the corporate are installed in the city and have branches scattered in several of its centrality. So Paulo is the home of the 75% of the main fairs of the country. The city also promotes one of the most important fashion weeks in the world,
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Fashion_Week" title="So Paulo Fashion Week">
       So Paulo Fashion Week
      </a>
      , established in 1996 under the name Morumbi Fashion Brasil, is the largest and most important fashion event in Latin America.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Besides, the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="So Paulo Gay Pride Parade">
       So Paulo Gay Pride Parade
      </a>
      , held since 1997 on
      <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">
       Paulista Avenue
      </a>
      towards combating
      <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">
       homophobia
      </a>
      , is the event that attracts more tourists to the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cultural tourism also has relevance to the city, especially when taking into view the various international events that take place in the metropolis, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="So Paulo Art Biennial">
       So Paulo Art Biennial
      </a>
      , that attracted almost 1 million people in 2004. It represented a wide range of artistic positions. Its aims include an intensification of the North-South dialogue inside Brazil and promoting links between non-European cultures along a South-South orientation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The city has many cultural activities and a nightlife that is considered one of the best in the country. There are several cinemas, theaters, museums and cultural centers, some serving portion with greater purchasing power, others contemplating more popular audience, which leads many to say that "there is always a program to do in Sao Paulo." The
      <a href="/wiki/Rua_Oscar_Freire" title="Rua Oscar Freire">
       Rua Oscar Freire
      </a>
      was named one of the eight most luxurious streets in the world, according to the Mystery Shopping International,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oscar_Freire_91-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Oscar_Freire-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and So Paulo the 25th "most expensive city" of the planet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to the International Congress &amp; Convention Association (ICCA), So Paulo ranks first among the cities that host international events in
      <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
       Americas
      </a>
      and the 12th in the world, after the
      <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">
       Vienna
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
       Paris
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
       Barcelona
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
       Singapore
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
       Berlin
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">
       Budapest
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">
       Amsterdam
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">
       Stockholm
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">
       Seoul
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">
       Lisbon
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copenhague" title="Copenhague">
       Copenhague
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to a study by
      <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" title="MasterCard">
       MasterCard
      </a>
      in 130 cities around the world, So Paulo was the third most visited destination in Latin America (behind
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
       Mexico City
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
       Buenos Aires
      </a>
      ) with 2.4 million foreign travelers, who spent US$2.9 billion in 2013 (the highest among the cities in the region). In 2014,
      <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">
       CNN
      </a>
      ranked nightlife So Paulo as the fourth best in the world, behind
      <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">
       New York
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
       Berlin
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">
       Ibiza
      </a>
      , in
      <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
       Spain
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The diversity of peoples and cultures that built the city also makes the rich cuisine of the region is itself a major tourist attraction. This statement can be proved by the wide variety of gastronomic city, covering more than 62 cuisines across more than 12,000 restaurants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the 10th International Congress of Gastronomy, Hospitality and Tourism (Cihat) conducted in 1997, the city received the title of "World Gastronomy Capital" of a commission formed by representatives of 43 nations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:908px;">
      <div class="thumbinner">
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virada.jpg" title="2007 Virada Cultural, in Downtown So Paulo.">
         <img alt="" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="1990" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virada.jpg/900px-Virada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virada.jpg/1350px-Virada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virada.jpg/1800px-Virada.jpg 2x" width="900"/>
        </a>
