       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">
       Health care
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health care">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="850" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg/220px-Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg/330px-Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg/440px-Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_Hospital" title="Albert Einstein Hospital">
         Albert Einstein Hospital
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Brazil" title="Health in Brazil">
       Health in Brazil
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rede_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Saud%C3%A1vel" title="Rede So Paulo Saudvel">
       Rede So Paulo Saudvel
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo is the largest health care hub in Latin America. Among its hospitals are the Albert Einstein Israelites Hospital, ranked as the best in Latin America and the
      <a href="/wiki/Hospital_das_Cl%C3%ADnicas_da_Universidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Hospital das Clnicas da Universidade de So Paulo">
       Hospital das Clnicas
      </a>
      , the largest in the region. The private health care sector is very large and most of Brazil's best hospitals are located in the city. As of September 2009, the city of So Paulo had:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       32,553
       <a href="/wiki/Ambulatory" title="Ambulatory">
        ambulatory
       </a>
       clinics, centers and professional offices (physicians, dentists and others);
      </li>
      <li>
       217 hospitals, with 32,554 beds;
      </li>
      <li>
       137,745 health care professionals, including 28,316 physicians.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1299" data-file-width="1890" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg/220px-Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg/330px-Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg/440px-Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hospitaldocancerdesp1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Cancer_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Institute of Cancer of So Paulo">
         Institute of Cancer of So Paulo
        </a>
        is the largest hospital of cancer in Brazil.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
         <a href="#cite_note-109">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          109
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_health">
       Municipal health
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Municipal health">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The municipal government operates public health facilities across the city's territory, with a total of 770 basic health care units (UBS), ambulatory and emergency clinics and 17 hospitals. The Municipal Secretary of Health has 59,000 employees, including more than 8,000 physicians and 12,000 nurses.
     </p>
     <p>
      More than 6,000,000 citizens uses these facilities, which provide drugs at no cost and manage an extensive family health program (PSF Programa de Sade da Famlia).
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Rede_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Saud%C3%A1vel" title="Rede So Paulo Saudvel">
       Rede So Paulo Saudvel
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Healthy So Paulo Network
      </i>
      ) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">
       satellite
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">
       digital TV
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Corporate_video" title="Corporate video">
       corporate channel
      </a>
      , developed by the Municipal Health Secretary of So Paulo, bringing programs focused on
      <a href="/wiki/Health_promotion" title="Health promotion">
       health promotion
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Health_education" title="Health education">
       health education
      </a>
      , which may be watched by citizens seeking health care in its units in the city.
     </p>
     <p>
      The network consists of two studios and a system for transmission of closed
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_video" title="Digital video">
       digital video
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">
       high definition
      </a>
      via
      <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">
       satellite
      </a>
      , with about 1,400 points of reception in all health care units of the municipality of So Paulo.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
       Transport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Margtiete.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="720" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Margtiete.jpg/220px-Margtiete.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Margtiete.jpg/330px-Margtiete.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Margtiete.jpg/440px-Margtiete.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Margtiete.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Marginal_Tiet%C3%AA" title="Marginal Tiet">
         Marginal Tiet
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="445" data-file-width="667" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg/220px-Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg/330px-Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg/440px-Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rodovia_Bandeirantes_SAO_2008_06.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Rodovia dos Bandeirantes">
         Rodovia dos Bandeirantes
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG/220px-Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG/330px-Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG/440px-Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Rodoanel_M%C3%A1rio_Covas" title="Rodoanel Mrio Covas">
         Rodoanel Mrio Covas
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Transport in So Paulo">
       Transport in So Paulo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Brazil" title="Transport in Brazil">
       Transport in Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Automobiles are still the main means to get into the city. In March 2011, more than 7 million vehicles were registered.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Heavy traffic is common on the city's main avenues and
      <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">
       traffic jams
      </a>
      are relatively common on its highways.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">
       Highways
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Highways">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The city is crossed by 10 major motorways:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Presidente_Dutra" title="Rodovia Presidente Dutra">
        Rodovia Presidente Dutra
       </a>
       /BR-116 (President Dutra Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the east and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordinal_direction" title="Ordinal direction">
        north-east
       </a>
       of the country. Most important connection:
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
        Rio de Janeiro
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Rodovia Rgis Bittencourt/BR-116 (Rgis Bittencourt Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the south of the country. Most important connections:
       <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">
        Curitiba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">
        Porto Alegre
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Fern%C3%A3o_Dias" title="Rodovia Ferno Dias">
        Rodovia Ferno Dias
       </a>
       /BR-381 (Ferno Dias Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the north of the country. Most important connection:
       <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">
        Belo Horizonte
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Anchieta" title="Rodovia Anchieta">
        Rodovia Anchieta
       </a>
       /SP-150 (Anchieta Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the ocean coast. Mainly used for cargo transportation to
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santos" title="Port of Santos">
        Santos Port
       </a>
       . Most important connection:
       <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, So Paulo">
        Santos
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Imigrantes" title="Rodovia dos Imigrantes">
        Rodovia dos Imigrantes
       </a>
       /SP-150 (Immigrants Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the ocean coast. Mainly used for tourism. Most important connections: Santos,
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="So Vicente, So Paulo">
        So Vicente
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guaruj%C3%A1" title="Guaruj">
        Guaruj
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Praia_Grande" title="Praia Grande">
        Praia Grande
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Castelo_Branco" title="Rodovia Castelo Branco">
        Rodovia Castelo Branco
       </a>
       /SP-280 (President Castelo Branco Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the west and
       <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_direction" title="Cardinal direction">
        north-west
       </a>
       of the country. Most important connections:
       <a href="/wiki/Osasco" title="Osasco">
        Osasco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sorocaba" title="Sorocaba">
        Sorocaba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bauru" title="Bauru">
        Bauru
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%BA" title="Ja">
        Ja
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Campo_Grande" title="Campo Grande">
        Campo Grande
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Raposo_Tavares" title="Rodovia Raposo Tavares">
        Rodovia Raposo Tavares
       </a>
       /SP-270 (Raposo Tavares Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the west of the country. Most important connections:
       <a href="/wiki/Cotia" title="Cotia">
        Cotia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sorocaba" title="Sorocaba">
        Sorocaba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Presidente_Prudente,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Presidente Prudente, So Paulo">
        Presidente Prudente
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Anhanguera" title="Rodovia Anhanguera">
        Rodovia Anhangera
       </a>
       /SP-330 (Anhanguera Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the north-west of the country, including its capital city. Most important connections:
       <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">
        Campinas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ribeir%C3%A3o_Preto" title="Ribeiro Preto">
        Ribeiro Preto
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Braslia">
        Braslia
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Rodovia dos Bandeirantes">
        Rodovia dos Bandeirantes
       </a>
       /SP-348 (Bandeirantes Highway)  Connects So Paulo to the north-west of the country. It is considered the best motorway of Brazil. Most important connections:
       <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">
        Campinas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ribeir%C3%A3o_Preto" title="Ribeiro Preto">
        Ribeiro Preto
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Piracicaba" title="Piracicaba">
        Piracicaba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_do_Rio_Preto" title="So Jos do Rio Preto">
        So Jos do Rio Preto
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Ayrton_Senna" title="Rodovia Ayrton Senna">
        Rodovia Ayrton Senna
       </a>
       /SP-70 (Ayrton Senna Highway)  Named after Brazilian legendary
       <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">
        Formula One
       </a>
       pilot
       <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">
        Ayrton Senna
       </a>
       , this motorway connects So Paulo to east locations of the state, as well as the north coast of the state. Most important connections:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo-Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="So Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport">
        So Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_dos_Campos" title="So Jos dos Campos">
        So Jos dos Campos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Caraguatatuba" title="Caraguatatuba">
        Caraguatatuba
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rodoanel">
       Rodoanel
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Rodoanel">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Rodoanel_M%C3%A1rio_Covas" title="Rodoanel Mrio Covas">
       Rodoanel Mrio Covas
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      From the 1940s to the 1980s, many roads and buildings were built without major planning. Ex-governor
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Covas" title="Mrio Covas">
       Mrio Covas
      </a>
      sponsored a ring road that circles the city, called Rodoanel Mario Covas,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is being built by DERSA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">
       Railways
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Railways">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1825" data-file-width="2229" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/220px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/330px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/440px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Luz,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Luz_Station" title="Luz Station">
         Luz Station
        </a>
        "Estao da Luz."
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Brazil" title="Rail transport in Brazil">
       Rail transport in Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The two major So Paulo
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_stations" title="Railway stations">
       railway stations
      </a>
      are Luz and Julio Prestes in the Luz/Campos Eliseos region. Luz is the seat of the Santos-
      <a href="/wiki/Jundia%C3%AD" title="Jundia">
       Jundia
      </a>
      line which historically transported
      <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">
       international immigrants
      </a>
      from the Santos port to So Paulo and the coffee plantation lands in the Western region of
      <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">
       Campinas
      </a>
      . Julio Prestes connected Southwest So Paulo State and Northern
      <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paran (state)">
       Paran
      </a>
      State to So Paulo. Agricultural products were transferred to Luz Station from which they headed to the
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
       Atlantic ocean
      </a>
      and overseas. Julio Prestes stopped transporting passengers through the Sorocabana or FEPASA lines and now only has limited suburban service. Due to its acoustics and interior beauty, surrounded by Greek revival columns, part of the rebuilt station was transformed into the So Paulo Hall.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Luz_Station" title="Luz Station">
       Luz Station
      </a>
      was built in Britain and assembled in Brazil. It has an underground station and is still very active with east and westbound suburban trains that link So Paulo to the Greater So Paulo region to the East and the Campinas Metropolitan region in Jundia in the western part of the State. Besides housing the interactive
      <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">
       Museu da Lngua Portuguesa
      </a>
      (Portuguese Language Museum), Luz Station is surrounded by important
      <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">
       cultural
      </a>
      institutions such as the Pinacoteca do Estado, The Museu de Arte Sacra on Tiradentes Avenue and Jardim da Luz, among others.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg/220px-CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg/330px-CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg/440px-CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CPTM_2071_VOL.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Train of the
        <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">
         CPTM
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Although poorly maintained by heavy rail services, a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio%E2%80%93S%C3%A3o_Paulo_High-speed_rail" title="RioSo Paulo High-speed rail">
       high-speed railway
      </a>
      service is proposed to link So Paulo and Rio de Janeiro.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The trains are projected to reach 280 kilometres per hour (170mph), taking about 90 minutes.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another important project is the "Expresso Bandeirantes," a medium-speed rail service (about 160km/h) from So Paulo to
      <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">
       Campinas
      </a>
      , which would reduce the journey time from 90 minutes by car to about 50 minutes, linking So Paulo,
      <a href="/wiki/Jundia%C3%AD" title="Jundia">
       Jundia
      </a>
      , Campinas Airport and Campinas city center. This service is also to connect to the railway service between So Paulo city center and Guarulhos Airport. Work on an express railway service between So Paulo city center and Guarulhos International Airport were announced by the So Paulo state government in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
       Airports
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airports">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2691" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg/220px-Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg/330px-Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg/440px-Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congonhas-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Airport" title="Congonhas-So Paulo Airport">
         Congonhas Airport
        </a>
        serves domestic flights.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo has two main airports,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo-Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="So Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport">
       So Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">
       IATA
      </a>
      :
      <b>
       GRU
      </b>
      ) for international flights and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congonhas-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Airport" title="Congonhas-So Paulo Airport">
       Congonhas-So Paulo Airport
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">
       IATA
      </a>
      :
      <b>
       CGH
      </b>
      ) for domestic and regional flights. Another airport, the
      <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Marte_Airport" title="Campo de Marte Airport">
       Campo de Marte Airport
      </a>
      , serves light aircraft. The three airports together moved 42,617,779 passengers in 2010, making So Paulo one of the top 20 busiest in the world, by number of air passenger movements. The region of Greater So Paulo is also served by
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_dos_Campos_Airport" title="So Jos dos Campos Airport">
       So Jos dos Campos Airport
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viracopos-Campinas_International_Airport" title="Viracopos-Campinas International Airport">
       Viracopos-Campinas International Airport
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Congonhas Airport operates flights mainly to Rio de Janeiro, Belo Horizonte and Braslia. In the latest upgrade, eight
      <a href="/wiki/Boarding_(transport)" title="Boarding (transport)">
       boarding
      </a>
      bridges were installed to provide more comfort to passengers by eliminating the need to walk in the open to their flights. The terminal area was expanded from 37.3 thousand to over 51 thousand square meters. This expansion was to satisfy current demand rather than to raise capacity. Built in the 1930s, it was designed to handle 6 million passengers a year and was struggling to handle 12million instead.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      So Paulo-Guarulhos International, also known as "Cumbica" is 25km (16mi) north-east of the city center, in the neighbouring city of
      <a href="/wiki/Guarulhos" title="Guarulhos">
       Guarulhos
      </a>
      . Every day nearly 100 thousand people pass through the airport, which connects Brazil to 28 countries around the world. 370 companies operate there, generating 53 thousand jobs. With capacity to serve 15million passengers a year, in two terminals, the airport currently handles 32million users.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3194" data-file-width="5022" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/220px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/330px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/440px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo-Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="So Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport">
         So Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport
        </a>
        is the largest airport in Latin America and Southern Hemisphere.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
         <a href="#cite_note-116">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          116
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Construction of a third passenger terminal is pending, to raise yearly capacity to more than 60million passengers. The project, in the financing phase, is part of the airports master plan and will get under way shortly. So Paulo International Airport is also the main
      <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Earth" title="Atmosphere of Earth">
       air
      </a>
      cargo
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_hub" title="Transport hub">
       hubs
      </a>
      in Brazil. The roughly 100 flights a day carry everything from fruits grown in the So Francisco Valley to locally manufactured medicine. The airport's cargo terminal is South America's largest. In 2003, over 75 thousand metric tons of freight passed through the terminal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Campo de Marte is located in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santana_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Santana (So Paulo)">
       Santana
      </a>
      district, the northern
      <a href="/wiki/Zoning" title="Zoning">
       zone
      </a>
      of So Paulo. The airport handles small aircraft, including
      <a href="/wiki/Air_taxi" title="Air taxi">
       air taxi
      </a>
      firms. Opened in 1935, Campo de Marte is the base for the largest helicopter fleet in Brazil. It has no scheduled service, but its terminal is equipped with a snack bar, restaurant and bank branch. This airport is the home base of the State Civil Police Air Tactical Unit, the State Military Police Radio Patrol Unit and the So Paulo Flying Club.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Largely using this airport, prosperous passengers take advantage of some one hundred remote helipads and heliports to conveniently bypass heavy road traffic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Campo de Marte also hosts the Ventura
      <a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Blimp" title="Goodyear Blimp">
       Goodyear Blimp
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">
       Metro
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Metro">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="935" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg/220px-Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg/330px-Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg/440px-Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Commuter_Train_or_Subway%3F%3F%3F.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        So Paulo Metro was elected the best metro in the
        <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
         Americas
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
         <a href="#cite_note-120">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          120
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="So Paulo Metro">
       So Paulo Metro
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">
       Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo has three rapid transport systems: the underground
      <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">
       rail system
      </a>
      (called "metr", short for "metropolitano" and in plates in English is called "subway"), with five lines; the
      <a href="/wiki/Regional_rail" title="Regional rail">
       suburban rail
      </a>
      system,
      <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">
       Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos
      </a>
      (CPTM), has six lines that serve many regions not reached by the underground system and even some other cities in the metropolitan region; and the CPTM network is longer than the underground rail system. The fast-lane bus system: there are many such bus lines in the city, called "Passa Rpido," which are street-level, placed on large avenues and connected with the underground or suburban train stations.
     </p>
     <p>
      The city currently has 379 kilometres (235mi) of rail operated by three companies. The
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="So Paulo Metro">
       So Paulo Metro
      </a>
      operates 69.0km (42.9mi) of underground railway systems (34.6km (21.5mi) fully underground)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      locally known as the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="So Paulo Metro">
       Metr
      </a>
      ), with 5 lines in operation and 59 stations.
      <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">
       Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos
      </a>
      (CPTM, or "Paulista Company of Metropolitan Trains") railway add 260.7km (162.0mi). The third company is Via4. The underground and railway lines carry some 7 million people on an average weekday. New underground lines are expected to move another million people per day within the next five years. The projects would expand So Paulo's
      <a href="/wiki/Urban_rail_transit" title="Urban rail transit">
       urban railway
      </a>
      system from the current 322km (200mi) to more than 500km (310mi) on the next 10 years, surpassing the
      <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">
       London Underground
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monotrilho_de_SP_(2).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1943" data-file-width="2589" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Monotrilho_de_SP_%282%29.jpg/220px-Monotrilho_de_SP_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Monotrilho_de_SP_%282%29.jpg/330px-Monotrilho_de_SP_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Monotrilho_de_SP_%282%29.jpg/440px-Monotrilho_de_SP_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monotrilho_de_SP_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">
         monorail
        </a>
        line 15 subway.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Expresso_Tiradentes" title="Expresso Tiradentes">
       Expresso Tiradentes
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo has no tram lines, although trams were common in the first half of the 20th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      So Paulo's underground train system is overcrowded, but was certified by the NBR
      <a href="/wiki/ISO_9000" title="ISO 9000">
       ISO 9001
      </a>
      . It has five lines and links to the metropolitan train network. The So Paulo Metro last year
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
         <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2014)">
          when?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      reached the mark of 11.5million passengers on mile of line, 15% higher than in 2008, when 10 million users were taken per mile. It is the largest concentration of people in a single transport system in the world, according to the company.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      While the total number of passengers increased, satisfaction decreased. The survey "The Metro according to its user: a service evaluation" of last year showed that 60% of respondents rated the means of transport as "very good" and "good." In 2009, the notes were 67% positive.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">
       Buses
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Buses">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg/220px-Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg/330px-Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg/440px-Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_Bus_Terminal" title="Tiet Bus Terminal">
         Tiet Bus Terminal
        </a>
        , the second largest
        <a href="/wiki/Bus_station" title="Bus station">
         Bus Terminal
        </a>
        in the World. After only
        <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Bus_Terminal" title="Port Authority Bus Terminal">
         New York Port Authority Bus Terminal
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
         <a href="#cite_note-125">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          125
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Trolleybuses in So Paulo">
       Trolleybuses in So Paulo
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Bus transport (government and private) is composed of approximately 17,000 buses (including about 290
      <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
       trolley buses
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juts2009_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-juts2009-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The traditional system of informal transport (dab vans) was later reorganized and legalized under a consistent set of rules.
     </p>
     <p>
      So Paulo
      <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_Bus_Terminal" title="Tiet Bus Terminal">
       Tiet Bus Terminal
      </a>
      is the second largest bus terminal in the world. It serves localities across the nation, with the exception of the states of
      <a href="/wiki/Amazonas_(Brazilian_state)" title="Amazonas (Brazilian state)">
       Amazonas
      </a>
      , Roraima and
      <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amap">
       Amap
      </a>
      . Routes to 1,010 cities in five countries (Brazil, Argentina, Chile, Uruguay and Paraguay) are available. It connects to all regional airports and a
      <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">
       ride sharing
      </a>
      automobile service to
      <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, So Paulo">
       Santos
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Palmeiras-Barra_Funda_Intermodal_Terminal" title="Palmeiras-Barra Funda Intermodal Terminal">
       Palmeiras-Barra Funda Intermodal Terminal
      </a>
      is much smaller and is connected to the Palmeiras-Barra Funda metro and Palmeiras-Barra Funda CPTM stations. It serves the southwestern cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Sorocaba" title="Sorocaba">
       Sorocaba
      </a>
      , Itapetininga, Itu, Botucatu,
      <a href="/wiki/Bauru" title="Bauru">
       Bauru
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADlia" title="Marlia">
       Marlia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%BA" title="Ja">
       Ja
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Avar%C3%A9,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Avar, So Paulo">
       Avar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Piraju" title="Piraju">
       Piraju
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_do_Rio_Pardo" title="Santa Cruz do Rio Pardo">
       Santa Cruz do Rio Pardo
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ipaussu" title="Ipaussu">
       Ipaussu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chavantes" title="Chavantes">
       Chavantes
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ourinhos" title="Ourinhos">
       Ourinhos
      </a>
      (on the border with
      <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paran (state)">
       Paran
      </a>
      State). It also serves
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_do_Rio_Preto" title="So Jos do Rio Preto">
       So Jos do Rio Preto
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ara%C3%A7atuba" title="Araatuba">
       Araatuba
      </a>
      and other small towns located on the northwest of So Paulo State.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG/220px-Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG/330px-Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG/440px-Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Helicoptero_sobre_a_prefeitura_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">
         Helicopter
        </a>
        arriving in the
        <a href="/wiki/Matarazzo_Building" title="Matarazzo Building">
         So Paulo City Hall
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Buses to So Paulo coast are available at the
      <a href="/wiki/Jabaquara_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Jabaquara (So Paulo Metro)">
       Jabaquara metro station
      </a>
      , which is the final southbound stop on
      <a href="/wiki/Line_1_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 1 (So Paulo Metro)">
       Line 1 (Blue)
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="So Paulo Metro">
       So Paulo Metro
      </a>
      . The Litoral bus terminal serves
      <a href="/wiki/Praia_Grande" title="Praia Grande">
       Praia Grande
      </a>
      , Santos and
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="So Vicente, So Paulo">
       So Vicente
      </a>
      on the South Shore and
      <a href="/wiki/Mongagu%C3%A1" title="Mongagu">
       Mongagu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bertioga" title="Bertioga">
       Bertioga
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Guaruj%C3%A1" title="Guaruj">
       Guaruj
      </a>
      on the North Shore. Buses to North Shore cities such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maresia" title="Maresia">
       Maresia
      </a>
      , Riviera de So Loureno,
      <a href="/wiki/Caraguatatuba" title="Caraguatatuba">
       Caraguatatuba
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ubatuba" title="Ubatuba">
       Ubatuba
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Paraty" title="Paraty">
       Paraty
      </a>
      , in
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">
       Rio de Janeiro
      </a>
      State must be taken at the
      <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_Bus_Terminal" title="Tiet Bus Terminal">
       Tiet Bus Terminal
      </a>
      , at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguesa-Tiet%C3%AA_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Portuguesa-Tiet (So Paulo Metro)">
       Portuguesa-Tiet metro station
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Line_1_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 1 (So Paulo Metro)">
       Line 1 (Blue)
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On October 26, 2013, hundreds of people attacked the bus station in So Paulo, setting fire to a bus and destroying cash and ticket machines. At least six people were arrested in the protests.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Helicopters">
       Helicopters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Helicopters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      So Paulo has the largest number of
      <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">
       helicopters
      </a>
      in the world. The second and third positions are of
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York City
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
       Tokyo
      </a>
      . With 420 helicopters
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in 2012 and around 2,000 flights per day within the central area, the city is turning into a "real life South-American episode" of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Jetsons" title="The Jetsons">
       The Jetsons
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Helicopters enable businessmen and other affluent workers to sharply reduce time spent moving around and commuting. Some companies own their helicopters, others lease them and still others use
      <a href="/wiki/Air_taxi" title="Air taxi">
       helicopter taxi
      </a>
      services. One suburban helicopter shuttle service, located about 15 miles (24km) from the center of the city in Tambor, is operated totally by women, including its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aviator" title="Aviator">
       pilots
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
       Music
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Music">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Brazil" title="Music of Brazil">
       Music of Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6375" data-file-width="17895" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/330px-Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/495px-Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/660px-Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="330"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Sala So Paulo">
         Sala So Paulo
        </a>
        , the home of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_State_Symphony" title="So Paulo State Symphony">
         So Paulo State Symphony
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Adoniran_Barbosa" title="Adoniran Barbosa">
       Adoniran Barbosa
      </a>
      was a
      <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">
       samba
      </a>
      singer and composer who became successful during So Paulo's early radio era. Born in 1912 in the town of
      <a href="/wiki/Valinhos" title="Valinhos">
       Valinhos
      </a>
      , Barbosa was known as the "composer to the masses", particularly Italian immigrants living in the quarters of Bela Vista, also known as "Bexiga" and Brs, as well as those who lived in the city's many 'cortios' or tenements. His songs drew from the life of urban workers, the unemployed and those who lived on the edge. His first big hit was "Saudosa Maloca" ("Shanty of Fond Memories"  1951), wherein three homeless friends recall with nostalgia their improvised shanty home, which was torn down by the landowner to make room for a building. His 1964
      <a href="/wiki/Trem_das_Onze" title="Trem das Onze">
       Trem das Onze
      </a>
      ("The 11pm Train"), became one of the five best samba songs ever, the protagonist explains to his lover that he cannot stay any longer because he has to catch the last train to the
      <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%A7an%C3%A3_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Jaan (district of So Paulo)">
       Jaan suburb
      </a>
      , for his mother will not sleep before he arrives home. Another important musician with a similar style is
      <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Vanzolini" title="Paulo Vanzolini">
       Paulo Vanzolini
      </a>
      . Vanzolini is a PhD in Biology and a part-time professional musician. He composed a song depicting a love murder scene in So Paulo called "Ronda".
     </p>
     <p>
      In the late 1960s, a psychedelic rock band called
      <a href="/wiki/Os_Mutantes" title="Os Mutantes">
       Os Mutantes
      </a>
      became popular. Their success is related to that of other
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropicalismo" title="Tropicalismo">
       tropicalia
      </a>
      musicians. The group were known as very
      <i>
       paulistanos
      </i>
      in their behaviour and clothing. Os Mutantes released five albums before lead singer
      <a href="/wiki/Rita_Lee" title="Rita Lee">
       Rita Lee
      </a>
      departed in 1972 to join another group called
      <a href="/wiki/Tutti_Frutti_(Brazilian_band)" title="Tutti Frutti (Brazilian band)">
       Tutti Frutti
      </a>
      . Although initially known only in Brazil, Os Mutantes became successful abroad after the 1990s. In 2000,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tecnicolor" title="Tecnicolor">
        Tecnicolor
       </a>
      </i>
      , an album recorded in the early 1970s in English by the band, was released with artwork designed by
      <a href="/wiki/Sean_Lennon" title="Sean Lennon">
       Sean Lennon
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="1840" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg/220px-Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg/330px-Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg/440px-Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Auditorium" title="Ibirapuera Auditorium">
         Ibirapuera Auditorium
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the early 1980s, a band called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ultraje_a_Rigor" title="Ultraje a Rigor">
        Ultraje a Rigor
       </a>
      </i>
      (Elegant Outrage) emerged. They played a simple and irreverent style of rock. The lyrics depicted the changes in society and culture that Brazilian society was experiencing. A late punk and garage scene became strong in the 1980s, perhaps associated with the gloomy scenario of unemployment during an extended recession. Bands originating from this movement include
      <a href="/wiki/Ira!" title="Ira!">
       Ira!
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tit%C3%A3s" title="Tits">
       Tits
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ratos_de_Por%C3%A3o" title="Ratos de Poro">
       Ratos de Poro
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Inocentes" title="Inocentes">
       Inocentes
      </a>
      . In the 1990s,
      <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">
       drum and bass
      </a>
      arose as another musical movement in So Paulo, with artists such as
      <a href="/wiki/DJ_Marky" title="DJ Marky">
       DJ Marky
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/DJ_Patife" title="DJ Patife">
       DJ Patife
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_de_Oliveira" title="Xerxes de Oliveira">
       XRS
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Drumagick" title="Drumagick">
       Drumagick
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fernanda_Porto" title="Fernanda Porto">
       Fernanda Porto
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many
      <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">
       heavy metal
      </a>
      bands also originated in So Paulo, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Angra_(band)" title="Angra (band)">
       Angra
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Torture_Squad" title="Torture Squad">
       Torture Squad
      </a>
      , Korzus and
      <a href="/wiki/Dr._Sin" title="Dr. Sin">
       Dr. Sin
      </a>
      . Famous electro-pop band
      <a href="/wiki/CSS_(band)" title="CSS (band)">
       Cansei de Ser Sexy
      </a>
      , or CSS (Portuguese for "tired of being sexy") also has its origins in the city.
     </p>
     <p>
      Many of the most important classical Brazilian living composers, such as Amaral Vieira,
      <a href="/wiki/Osvaldo_Lacerda" title="Osvaldo Lacerda">
       Osvaldo Lacerda
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Edson_Zampronha" title="Edson Zampronha">
       Edson Zampronha
      </a>
      , were born and live in So Paulo. Local
      <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">
       baritone
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Szot" title="Paulo Szot">
       Paulo Szot
      </a>
      has won international acclaim and a
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">
       Tony Award
      </a>
      nomination for his performance in a 2008 revival of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_(musical)" title="South Pacific (musical)">
        South Pacific
       </a>
      </i>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Orquestra_Sinf%C3%B4nica_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Orquestra Sinfnica do Estado de So Paulo">
       So Paulo State Symphony
      </a>
      is one of the world's outstanding orchestras; their artistic director beginning in 2012 is the noted American conductor
      <a href="/wiki/Marin_Alsop" title="Marin Alsop">
       Marin Alsop
      </a>
      . In 1952,
      <a href="/wiki/Heitor_Villa-Lobos" title="Heitor Villa-Lobos">
       Heitor Villa-Lobos
      </a>
      wrote his Symphony Number 10 ('Amerndia') for the 400th anniversary of So Paulo: an allegorical, historical and religious account of the city told through the eyes of its founder
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_de_Anchieta" title="Jose de Anchieta">
       Jose de Anchieta
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_halls_and_concert_halls">
       Music halls and concert halls
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music halls and concert halls">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Credicardhall.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1142" data-file-width="1417" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Credicardhall.jpg/220px-Credicardhall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Credicardhall.jpg/330px-Credicardhall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Credicardhall.jpg/440px-Credicardhall.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Credicardhall.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Citibank Hall.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo's most important opera houses are:
      <a href="/wiki/Theatro_Municipal_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Theatro Municipal (So Paulo)">
       So Paulo Municipal Theater
      </a>
      , Theatro So Pedro and Alfa Theater, for the symphonic concerts there is the
      <a href="/wiki/Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Sala So Paulo">
       Sala So Paulo
      </a>
      , the latter being the headquarters of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OSESP" title="OSESP">
       OSESP
      </a>
      , a notable orchestra. The city also hosts several music halls. The main ones are: Citibank Hall, HSBC Music Hall, Olympia, Via Funchal, Villa Country, Kezebre Rock Bar, Arena Anhembi and Espaco das Amricas. The
      <a href="/wiki/Sambadrome" title="Sambadrome">
       Sambadrome
      </a>
      hosts musical presentations as well.
     </p>
     <p>
      Other facilities include the new Praa das Artes, with the Municipal Conservatory of Music Chamber Hall and others venues, like, Cultura Artistica, Teatro Srgio Cardoso with a venue for only dance performances and Herzog &amp; DeMeron's Centro Cultural Luz, for Ballet, Opera, theater and concerts, with three huge halls. The auditorium of the Latin-American Cultural Center, The Mozarteum, holds concerts through the year.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
       Literature
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Literature">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg/220px-Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg/330px-Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg/440px-Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade_Library" title="Mrio de Andrade Library">
         Mrio de Andrade Library
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literature_of_Brazil" title="Literature of Brazil">
       Literature of Brazil
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      So Paulo was home to the first
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
       Jesuit
      </a>
      missionaries in Brazil, in the early 16th century. They wrote reports to the Portuguese crown about the newly found land, the
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
       native peoples
      </a>
      and composed poetry and music for the
      <a href="/wiki/Catechism" title="Catechism">
       catechism
      </a>
      , creating the first written works from the area. The literary priests included
      <a href="/wiki/Manuel_da_N%C3%B3brega" title="Manuel da Nbrega">
       Manuel da Nbrega
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="Jos de Anchieta">
       Jos de Anchieta
      </a>
      , living in or near the colony then called
      <i>
       Piratininga
      </i>
      . They also helped to register the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Tupi_language" title="Old Tupi language">
       Old Tupi language
      </a>
      , lexicon and its grammar.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1922, the Brazilian Modernist Movement, launched in So Paulo, began to achieve cultural independence. Brazil had gone through the same stages of development as the rest of Latin America, but its political and cultural
      <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">
       independence
      </a>
      came more gradually.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg/220px-Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg/330px-Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg/440px-Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bibliotecavictorcivita.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Victor_Civita_Latin_American_Library" title="Victor Civita Latin American Library">
         Victor Civita Latin American Library
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Brazilian elite culture was originally strongly tied to
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">
       Portugal
      </a>
      . Gradually writers developed a multi-ethnic body of work that was distinctively Brazilian. The presence of large numbers of former slaves added a distinctive
      <a href="/wiki/African_people" title="African people">
       African
      </a>
      character to the
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brazil" title="Culture of Brazil">
       culture
      </a>
      . Subsequent infusions of immigrants of non-Portuguese origin broadened the range of influences.
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade" title="Mrio de Andrade">
       Mrio de Andrade
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Oswald_de_Andrade" title="Oswald de Andrade">
       Oswald de Andrade
      </a>
      were the prototypical modernists. With the urban poems of "Paulicia Desvairada" and "Carefree Paulistan land" (1922), Mrio de Andrade established the
      <a href="/wiki/Cultural_movement" title="Cultural movement">
       movement
      </a>
      in Brazil. His rhapsodic novel
      <i>
       Macunama
      </i>
      (1928), with its abundance of Brazilian
      <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">
       folklore
      </a>
      , represents the apex of
      <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">
       modernism
      </a>
      's nationalist prose through its creation of an offbeat native
      <a href="/wiki/Hero" title="Hero">
       national hero
      </a>
      . Oswald de Andrade's experimental poetry,
      <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">
       avant-garde
      </a>
      prose, particularly the novel Serafim Ponte Grande (1933) and provocative manifestos exemplify the movement's break with tradition. Modernist artists and writers chose the Municipal Theatre of So Paulo to launch their Modernist manifesto. The site happened to be a bastion of European culture with opera and classical music presentations from Germany, France, Austria and Italy. They defied the high society that frequented the venue and who insisted on speaking only foreign languages such as French, behaving as if Brazilian culture did not matter.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Theaters">
       Theaters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Theaters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7210" data-file-width="11224" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg/220px-Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg/330px-Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg/440px-Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Theatro_Municipal_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Theatro Municipal (So Paulo)">
         Municipal Theatre of So Paulo
        </a>
        , "Teatro Municipal de So Paulo."
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Many historians believe that the first theatrical performance in Brazil was held in So Paulo. The Portuguese
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
       Jesuit
      </a>
      missionary
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="Jos de Anchieta">
       Jos de Anchieta
      </a>
      (15341597) wrote short plays that were performed and watched by the TupiGuarani natives. In the second half of the 19th century a cultural, musical and theatrical life emerged.
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">
       European ethnic groups
      </a>
      began holding performances in some of the state's rural cities. The most important period for the art in So Paulo was the 1940s. So Paulo had had a professional company, Teatro Brasileiro de Comdia, (Brazilian Theater of Comedy), along with others. During the 1960s, major theater productions in So Paulo and Brazil were presented by two groups. Teatro de Arena began with a group of students from Escola de Arte Dramtica (Drama
      <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">
       Art School
      </a>
      ), founded by Alfredo Mesquita, in 1948. In 1958, the group excelled with the play "Eles no usam black tie" by
      <a href="/wiki/Gianfrancesco_Guarnieri" title="Gianfrancesco Guarnieri">
       Gianfrancesco Guarnieri
      </a>
      which was the first in the history of the Brazilian drama to feature
      <a href="/wiki/Wage_labour" title="Wage labour">
       labor
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Laborer" title="Laborer">
       workers
      </a>
      as
      <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">
       protagonists
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After the military coup of 1964, plays started focusing on
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil" title="History of Brazil">
       Brazilian history
      </a>
      (Zumbi, Tiradentes). Teatro de Arena and Teatro Oficina supported the democratic resistance during the
      <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">
       military dictatorship
      </a>
      period, marked by its censorship. The Tropicalist movement began there. A number of plays represented
      <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">
       historic
      </a>
      moments, notably "O Rei da Vela", "Galileu Galilei" (1968), "Na Sela das Cidades" (1969) and "Gracias Seor" (1972).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The district of Bixiga concentrates the greatest number of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theater" title="Theater">
       theaters
      </a>
      , almost 30 including the theaters that are closed for refurbishing or for other reasons. Some of the most important are Renault, Brigadeiro, Zaccaro,
      <a href="/wiki/Bibi_Ferreira" title="Bibi Ferreira">
       Bibi Ferreira
      </a>
      , Maria della Costa, Ruth Escobar, Opera, TBC, Imprensa, Oficina, gora, Cacilda Becker, Srgio Cardoso, do Bixiga, and Bandeirantes.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">
       Museums
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pinacoteca_SP.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Pinacoteca_SP.jpg/220px-Pinacoteca_SP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Pinacoteca_SP.jpg/330px-Pinacoteca_SP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Pinacoteca_SP.jpg/440px-Pinacoteca_SP.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pinacoteca_SP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
